Constants and Variables: Revelation and Intellect in Islamic Reasoning
Author concludes by distinguishing constants (thawabit) from variables (mutaghayyirat).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between thawabit (constants) and mutaghayyirat (variables) and apply this framework to identify when revelation is the primary source and when intellect exercises ijtihad.

Core Idea
Revelation governs ends and universals; intellect governs means and particulars.

The author concludes the passage by drawing a crucial epistemological boundary: revelation is the bedrock of constants (thawabit) — the unchanging goals and principles — while the intellect operates in the realm of variables (mutaghayyirat) — the flexible means and methods that adapt to time and place. This framework prevents both rigid literalism and unbridled rationalism and is directly applicable to usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two pillars
Find the sentence that says 'إن ركيزة الثوابت الوحي، وركيزة المتغيرات العقل' (the pillar of constants is revelation, and the pillar of variables is the intellect). Memorize this as the core distinction.
2
Clarify what each pillar governs
Notice that revelation (constants) deals with 'الأهداف والغايات' (goals and ends) and 'قضايا الأصول والكليات' (issues of principles and universals). The intellect (variables) deals with 'الوسائل والأساليب المتغيرة' (changing means and methods) and 'قضايا الفروع والجزئيات' (issues of branches and particulars).
3
Apply the framework to an example
Consider a concrete issue: Salat (prayer) is a constant obligation (thabit) established by revelation. The method of calculating prayer times is a variable (mutaghayyir), determined by the intellect using astronomy and observation. This shows how the framework works in practice.
4
Understand the practical reflection in Islamic education
Read the final paragraph: the human intellect interacts with the universe through contemplation and experimentation, fulfilling the vicegerent role 'في ضوء توجيهات الوحي وإرشاداته' (in light of the guidance of revelation). This shows that intellect is active but always under revelation's umbrella.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباب الثالث: الفصل الثالث - الوحي
الأولى إرشادنا إلى الوحي والتصديق بالنبوة.
الثانية: القيام بإدراك الموحى به وتفهمه.
وهذا كفيل ببيان أن لا تعارض بين علوم النقل وعلوم العقل
وهنا نلاحظ أن العقل بالنسبة إلى التربية الإسلامية طليق في حركته منضبط بالوحي، فيكبح جماحه عن الشطط أو الذهاب بعيداً خارج دائرة حركته فالوحي للعقل بمثابة صمام أمان يصونه عن الانزلاق فيما لا يعنيه، وينذره بنقطة الخطر. إذا ما تجازو حدود المناطق الآمنة.
ثانياً - دور الوحي في العقل
ويمكن تلخيص دور الوحي في العقل بالأدوار التالية:
1 - إيقاظ العقل: وهذا يتضح من خلال الآيات التي جاءت تحث العقل على القيام بعملياته العليا وهي كثيرة جداً (سبق إيراد جانب كبير منهـا عنـد الحديث عن العقل).
٢- تزكية العقل: حيث إن الإنسان مكون من عقل و جهل وشهوات تفد إليه من بيئته الخارجية فلا بد أن يقوم مصدر معصوم بعمل تقويم وتزكية لهذا العقل غير المعصوم نتيجة اختلاطه بهذه المؤثرات البيئية. ومثال ذلك قول الله سبحانه: ﴿وَلا تَتَّبِعِ الْهَوَى فَيُضِلَّكَ عَنْ سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ.. ﴾ [ص: ٢٦/٣٨].
تزكية العقل وتتم هذه التنمية العقلية من خلال النظر في منظومة الإسلام المتكاملة تشريعات وأحكاماً وأخلاقاً وقيماً ومبادئ عملية تعمل على تنمية وإنهاض العقل باتجاه اكتشاف السنن وتسخير الطبيعة وإعمار الحياة وبناء الحضارة. ولذلك فمن الطبيعي أن تلي عملية التنمية عمليتا التذكير والتزكية، عن طريق العلم الذي أولاه القرآن خاصة اهتماماً متميزاً، ترمز إليـه كلمة (اقرأ) كإيذان بافتتاح حضارة علمية شاملة، فيها البناء والإعمار، ،والإحياء، والإصلاح، والتجديد.
- حماية العقل ولما كان العقل أحد الضروريات الخمس فإن الإسلام قد صانه حين حَرَّم الخمر، وكذلك حَرَّم كل أمر من شأنه أن يؤدي إلى ذهاب العقل وفقدانه.
-٥ تحرير العقل وذلك انبثاق من فلسفة تحرير الإنسان جذرياً تمهيداً لتوحيد الله - تعالى - وعبوديته والقرآن مليء بالآيات التي تبين عدم تأثر المسلم بأعمال المجتمع الخاطئة فلا يخشاها ولا يحاكيها، مما يبعث على التحرير والإبداع معاً(۱) (سبق إيراد جملة من الآيات).
وحاصل القول: إن ركيزة الثوابت الوحي، وركيزة المتغيرات العقل. فالأهداف والغايات يمثلها محور الثوابت، أما المرونة والمتغيرات فتمثلها الوسائل والأساليب المتغيرة تبعاً للزمان والمكان. ولذا كان هذا منطقة عمل العقل. ومن ناحية أخرى يشتغل الوحي في قضايا الأصول والكليات، في حين يشتغل العقل في قضايا الفروع والجزئيات وذلك على نحو عام.
وينعكس ذلك عملياً في ميدان التربية الإسلامية على النحو التالي: يقوم العقل الإنساني بالتفاعل مع الكون بشتى صور التفاعل الإيجابي كالتأمل والتجريب لمحتوياته الحسية والإفادة من ذلك في أداء أدوار الإنسان الاستخلافية على الأرض، في ضوء توجيهات الوحي وإرشاداته.
Chapter Three, Section Three: Revelation
First: Guiding us to revelation and affirming prophethood.
Second: Undertaking the perception and understanding of what is revealed.
This suffices to show that there is no contradiction between transmitted sciences and rational sciences.
Here we note that intellect in relation to Islamic education is free in its movement but regulated by revelation, which restrains its excesses or going far outside its circle of movement. So revelation for the intellect is like a safety valve that protects it from slipping into what does not concern it and warns it at the point of danger if it exceeds the boundaries of safe zones.
Secondly: The Role of Revelation in the Intellect
The role of revelation in the intellect can be summarized in the following roles:
1 - Awakening the intellect: This is evident from the many verses that urge the intellect to perform its higher operations (a large part of which was previously cited when discussing the intellect).
2 - Purification of the intellect: Since man is composed of intellect, ignorance, and desires that come to him from his external environment, an infallible source must perform a process of correction and purification for this non-infallible intellect as a result of its mixing with these environmental influences. An example of that is the saying of God Almighty: "And do not follow desire, for it will lead you astray from the way of God..." [Sad: 38:26].
Development of the intellect: This intellectual development occurs through consideration of the integrated system of Islam: legislations, rulings, morals, values, and practical principles that work to develop and raise the intellect towards discovering the sunan (natural laws), harnessing nature, building civilization. Therefore, it is natural that the processes of reminder and purification follow the process of development, through knowledge to which the Qur'an gave special attention, symbolized by the word "Iqra'" (Read) as an announcement of the opening of a comprehensive scientific civilization, in which there is building, construction, revival, reform, and renewal.
- Protection of the intellect: Since the intellect is one of the five necessities, Islam protected it when it prohibited alcohol, and also prohibited everything that might lead to the loss and disappearance of the intellect.
-5 Liberation of the intellect: This emanates from the philosophy of radically liberating man as a prelude to the tawhid of God Almighty and His worship. The Qur'an is full of verses that show that the Muslim is not affected by the wrong deeds of society, not fearing them nor imitating them, which leads to liberation and creativity together (a number of verses were previously cited).
The conclusion: The pillar of constants is revelation, and the pillar of variables is the intellect. The goals and ends are represented by the axis of constants, while flexibility and variables are represented by the means and methods that change according to time and place. Hence, this is the field of the intellect's work. On the other hand, revelation operates in issues of principles and universals, while the intellect operates in issues of branches and particulars, in a general manner.
This is practically reflected in the field of Islamic education as follows: The human intellect interacts with the universe in various forms of positive interaction, such as contemplation and experimentation of its sensory contents, and benefiting from that in performing man's vicegerent roles on earth, in light of the guidance and directives of revelation.
Source pages p. 328

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological discussion of the relationship between divine revelation (al-wahy) and the human intellect (al-‘aql) within the framework of Islamic education. The author begins by stating two preliminary matters: first, that revelation guides us to itself and to the affirmation of prophethood; second, that we must undertake to perceive and understand what is revealed. This establishes that there is no contradiction between transmitted and rational sciences. Then, the author introduces the central point: the intellect in Islamic education is free in its movement but regulated by revelation, which acts as a safety valve, restraining excess and warning of danger.

Next, the author enumerates five specific roles of revelation regarding the intellect:
1. Awakening the intellect: Revelation contains verses that urge the intellect to perform its higher operations, energizing it.
2. Purification of the intellect: Because humans are composed of intellect, ignorance, and desires influenced by environment, revelation, being infallible, corrects and purifies the non-infallible intellect. The example is the verse forbidding following desire.
3. Development of the intellect: This occurs through the integrated system of Islam—its laws, morals, and values—which develop the intellect towards discovering natural laws, harnessing nature, and building civilization. The word "Iqra'" (Read) symbolizes this scientific civilization.
4. Protection of the intellect: Since intellect is one of the five essential necessities (al-daruriyyat al-khams), Islam protects it by prohibiting alcohol and anything that leads to its loss.
5. Liberation of the intellect: This stems from the philosophy of liberating man for tawhid. The Qur'an shows that Muslims should not be influenced by erroneous societal norms, fostering liberation and creativity.

Finally, the author concludes with a key principle: revelation is the basis of constants (thawabit), while the intellect is the basis of variables (mutaghayyirat). Goals and ends are constants, while means and methods are variables that change with time and place. Thus, revelation deals with universals and principles, while the intellect deals with particulars and branches. In practice, in Islamic education, the human intellect interacts with the universe through contemplation and experimentation, using sensory content, to fulfill man's role as vicegerent on earth, all within the guidance of revelation.

Key Terms

المتغيرات
الأهداف والغايات
الوسائل والأساليب
الأصول والكليات
الفروع والجزئيات

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following best represents the domain of revelation?
A) Changing means and methods
B) Issues of branches and particulars
C) Goals and ends
D) Contemplation and experimentation

Key Takeaway
Revelation provides fixed goals and universal principles; the intellect handles flexible means and particular applications.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Give an example from fiqh where the ruling is a constant (thabit) and the method of implementation is a variable (mutaghayyir). Explain how revelation and intellect each contribute.
?
In the context of Islamic finance, identify one constant principle (e.g., prohibition of riba) and one variable method (e.g., types of permissible contracts) and show how the intellect operates within the revealed boundary.

Critique of the Reason-Revelation Dichotomy
Author critiques the imported dichotomy between reason and transmitted knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the foreign origin of the false dichotomy between reason and revelation in Islamic thought and critique a contemporary example using the principle of complementarity.

Core Idea
The dichotomy between reason and revelation is a foreign import, not an Islamic reality.

In this lesson, we will explore the author's critique of the alleged opposition between reason and transmitted knowledge in Islam. The author argues that this dichotomy is not only false but also alien to the Islamic tradition, having been imported from Renaissance Europe. We will examine how the author refutes a contemporary educational writer who perpetuates this dichotomy, and learn to recognize the signs of civilizational alienation in such claims.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's thesis
Read the opening sentences to find the author's main claim: the relationship between revelation and transmission is one of mutual support and integration, not conflict. The dichotomy is fabricated.
Focus on the phrase 'لا مساغ ألبتة في افتعال ثنائية العقل والنقل'.
2
Trace the historical origin
The author traces the dichotomy to Renaissance Europe as a reaction to church authority. Note how the author distinguishes this European context from Islamic history.
Key phrase: 'المدرسة العقلية لم تنشأ إلا في أوروبا النهضة'.
3
Examine the contemporary example
The author quotes an educational writer who claims that 'traditionalists' (naqliyyun) confined knowledge to the unseen and restricted education to religious goals, and that after the Mutawakkil's coup, reason was defeated. Identify the specific historical references.
Pay attention to the mention of the Qadiri creed (413 AH) and the contrast with al-Ma'mun.
4
Analyze the author's refutation
The author rejects this as a product of cultural alienation and oversimplification. He questions whether such a battle ever occurred on that scale, and points out that individual differences do not constitute two opposing camps.
Look for the rhetorical question 'وهل سمع أحدنا بنشوب معركة أو معارك بهذا الحجم'.

Source Text

وإذ تبين لنا أن سمة العلاقة بين الوحي والنقل هي التعاضد والتكامل والتعانق، وأن الخلاف الذي دار بين الفرق الإسلامية وبعضها ليس حول حجيتهما أو أحدهما، وإنما حول مظاهر التعارض التي قد تبرز بينهما، فيلجؤون إلى البحث عن آلية في التأويل. إذا تبين ذلك فلا مساغ ألبتة في افتعال ثنائية العقل والنقل، لتقصى الأولى على حساب الأخرى أو العكس. إن انتقال هذه الثنائية إلى العالم الإسلامي غريب، وقد تسللت إليه غداة الغزوة الثقافية لديار المسلمين، والتي أدت إلى استلاب حضاري بات العقل المسلم يعاني من ضغطها إلى الحد الذي أفقده التوازن في معيارية القيمة، كما تسبب في إضعاف الرؤية عنده، وخلخة الصوابية في تصوره للقضايا وإصداره للأحكام. ولعل اختلاق هذه القضية بين العقل والنقل أبرز مظاهر أزمة العقل المسلم المعاصر بحق. وحين نؤكد على غرابة هذا المسلك في التفكير فإنما نشير بذلك إلى أن المدرسة العقلية لم تنشأ إلا في أوروبا النهضة، بدافع رد الفعل على سلطان الكنيسة، التي أوهنت العقل من جانب، ورد اعتبار للعقل الذي بدأت تسخر منه الاتجاهات الحسية لديهم من جانب آخر. وإذا عرفنا هذا فإن الأمر سيزداد غرابة حين نجد الترويج لهذه الثنائية مهيمناً على تفكير بعض الكتاب التربويين المعاصرين، ومن ذلك أن يتحدث أحدهم عن مصدر المعرفة فيقول: هكذا حسم النقليون الموقف من مصدر المعرفة والغرض منها، والسبيل إلى التماسها بأن ردوا كل ذلك إلى الغيب وقيدوا الغاية من التعليم بالهدف الديني الفرد الذي يقاس فيه الغائب على الشاهد، ثم عدوا العجز عن إدراكه مرضاً. وفي موطن لاحق من دراسته يعد الاعتراك قد وقع في الفكر الإسلامي غداة تلاقي العقل الإسلامي مع العقل اليوناني... هذا بإيمانياته وغيبياته وذاك بعقلانيته وموضوعيته ... قد يكون أمراً ثقيلاً على أفئدتنا أن نعترف بأن قوى المحافظة في الفكر التربوي العربي الإسلامي أفلحت بعد انقلاب المتوكل، وصدور كتاب الاعتقاد القادري سنة ٤١٣ هـ أن ترتد على عصر المأمون وتهزم العقل، والعقل البرهاني، ذلك ما أريد. وحديث كهذا يمثل شاهداً قوياً على ما ذكر آنفاً من مظاهر الاستلاب الحضاري لدى العقل المسلم المعاصر بحيث أضحى على هذا النحو من تصوره لمشكلة بمستوى مصادر المعرفة وطرائقها. وإذن فهل من المسلّم أن النقليين حسموا الموقف من مصدر المعرفة وما يتصل بها لمجرد أنهم آمنوا بالغيب وتقييدهم للتعليم بالهدف الديني، الذي يقاس فيه الغائب على الشاهد... إلخ. إن تقديم الموضوع بهذه الصورة تسطيح معيب الحقيقة الأمر، فإن التقسيم على هذا النحو (نقليون) و (عقليون) وكأنهما تياران متعارضان متناقضان لا لقاء بينهما ولا وفاق لا يمثل الحقيقة الموضوعية. بل هو يؤكد الوقوع في فخ الاستلاب الحضاري، المغاير للحقيقة التاريخية. وهل سمع أحدنا بنشوب معركة أو معارك بهذا الحجم بين تيار العقل وتيار النقل؟ أما أن يوجد عند آجاد العلماء في القديم أو الحديث، فذلك لا يرقى ليمثل اتجاهين متنافرين متناحرين، كما هذه الصورة عنهما الكاتب . رسم
And when it became clear to us that the characteristic of the relationship between revelation and transmitted knowledge is mutual support, integration, and interlocking, and that the disagreement that occurred among Islamic sects and among themselves was not about the authority of both or one of them, but rather about the manifestations of apparent contradiction that may arise between them, so they resort to searching for a mechanism of interpretation. When that became clear, there is absolutely no room for fabricating a dichotomy between reason and transmission, to prioritize the former over the latter or vice versa. Indeed, the transmission of this dichotomy into the Islamic world is strange, and it infiltrated it at the time of the cultural invasion of Muslim lands, which led to a civilizational alienation that the Muslim mind suffers from its pressure to the extent that it lost balance in the normativity of value, and also caused a weakening of vision in it, and a dislocation of correctness in its perception of issues and issuance of rulings. Perhaps the fabrication of this issue between reason and transmission is the most prominent manifestation of the crisis of the contemporary Muslim mind truly. And when we emphasize the strangeness of this path of thinking, we are thereby pointing out that the rationalist school did not arise except in Renaissance Europe, driven by a reaction to the authority of the church, which weakened reason on one side, and a restoration of consideration for reason that had begun to be mocked by empirical tendencies among them on the other side. And if we know this, then the matter becomes even stranger when we find the promotion of this dichotomy dominating the thinking of some contemporary educational writers, including that one of them speaks about the source of knowledge and says: 'Thus the traditionalists (naqliyyun) settled the position on the source of knowledge and its purpose and the way to seek it by returning all of that to the unseen and restricting the purpose of education to the individual religious goal in which the absent is compared to the present, then they considered inability to perceive it as a disease.' And in a later place in his study, he considers that the clash occurred in Islamic thought at the meeting of the Islamic mind with the Greek mind... this one with its beliefs and unseen matters, and that one with its rationalism and objectivity... it may be a heavy matter on our hearts to admit that the conservative forces in Arab-Islamic educational thought succeeded after the Mutawakkil's coup and the issuance of the Qadiri creed in 413 AH to retreat to the era of al-Ma'mun and defeat reason, and demonstrative reason, that is what was intended. And such speech represents a strong testimony to what was mentioned earlier of the manifestations of civilizational alienation in the contemporary Muslim mind to the extent that it has become like this in its perception of a problem at the level of sources of knowledge and their methods. So then, is it taken for granted that the traditionalists settled the matter of the source of knowledge and its related issues simply because they believed in the unseen and their restriction of education to the religious goal, in which the absent is measured by the present... etc? Presenting the subject in this way is a disgraceful oversimplification of the truth; for the division in this manner into 'traditionalists' and 'rationalists' as if they are two opposing contradictory currents with no meeting or agreement between them does not represent objective reality. Rather, it confirms falling into the trap of civilizational alienation, contrary to historical truth. Has any of us heard of a battle or battles of this magnitude between the current of reason and the current of transmission? But that it exists among individual scholars, ancient or modern, that does not rise to represent two conflicting hostile tendencies, as this writer has portrayed them.
Source pages p. 330

Commentary
This passage is a critical refutation of the alleged dichotomy between reason ('aql) and transmitted knowledge (naql) in Islamic thought. The author begins by establishing the correct Islamic view: revelation (wahy) and transmission (naql) are mutually supportive, integrated, and intertwined. Disagreements among Islamic schools were never about the authority of both but about how to handle apparent contradictions, leading to interpretive mechanisms. Therefore, there is no justification for fabricating a dichotomy that prioritizes one over the other. The author argues that this dichotomy is foreign to Islam, having infiltrated during the cultural invasion of Muslim lands, resulting in civilizational alienation. The rationalist school originated in Renaissance Europe as a reaction to church authority, not from within Islam. The author then provides a concrete example: a contemporary educational writer claims that the 'traditionalists' (naqliyyun) confined knowledge to the unseen and restricted education to religious goals, and later asserts that after the Mutawakkil’s coup and the Qadiri creed, conservative forces defeated reason. The author refutes this, calling it a product of cultural alienation. He asks whether such a battle between reason and transmission ever occurred in Islamic history on that scale. Individual differences among scholars do not constitute two opposing camps. The passage uses the principle of 'al-gha'ib 'ala al-shahid' (comparing the unseen to the witnessed) as a common tool in Islamic reasoning, not a flaw. In sum, the author defends the harmony of reason and revelation in Islam, warning against imported dichotomies.

Key Terms
الوحي
النقل
العقل
ثنائية
الاستلاب الحضاري

B) It was imported from Renaissance Europe as a reaction to church authority.
C) It dates back to the early Mu'tazilite and Ash'arite theological disputes.
D) It is a universal epistemological distinction found in all civilizations.

Key Takeaway
The false dichotomy between reason and revelation is a foreign import that undermines the true Islamic harmony between the two sources of knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Identify a contemporary claim from an educational or intellectual source that pits reason against revelation. Using the author's arguments, critique this claim by tracing its origin and showing how it misrepresents Islamic intellectual history.
?
Explain how the principle of 'al-gha'ib 'ala al-shahid' (comparing the unseen to the witnessed) is used in Islamic reasoning to integrate reason and revelation, using an example from tafsir or fiqh.

Rejecting the False Dichotomy Between Reason and Revelation
Author critiques the false dichotomy between 'aqli' and 'naqli' traditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and critique the false dichotomy between 'aqli' and 'naqli' in Islamic intellectual history, and distinguish it from legitimate epistemological categories.

Core Idea
The binary of 'rationalists' vs 'traditionalists' is a modern distortion, not the historical reality.

Many contemporary discussions of Islamic thought pit 'reason' against 'revelation' as if they are irreconcilable enemies. This passage from a modern scholar argues that this framing itself is a symptom of 'civilizational alienation' (istilab hadari) — an uncritical adoption of Western categories. The author acknowledges real periods of decline but insists that the simplistic binary obscures the nuanced, complementary relationship between reason and transmitted knowledge in classical Islam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the binary being critiqued
Locate where the author mentions the terms 'naqliyyun' and 'aqliyyun'. Note how he describes them: 'two opposing, contradictory currents with no meeting or agreement.'
2
Understand the concept of istilab hadari
The author claims that imposing this binary on Islamic history is a manifestation of 'civilizational alienation'. Reflect on what it means to adopt a foreign framework that distorts one's own intellectual heritage.
This is a modern critical term; classical scholars did not use it.
3
Recognize the author's nuanced position on taqlid and decline
The author does not deny that a 'flood of imitation' caused decline. He insists that rejecting the binary is not an apology for stagnation. Note his careful balance.
4
Identify the positive alternative
The author affirms domains where reason alone is insufficient, citing the details of the unseen (ghayb) and Ibn Taymiyya. This shows the complementary role of transmitted inference (istidlal naqli).
This aligns with classical positions like that of Ibn Taymiyya.

بنشوب معركة أو معارك بهذا الحجم بين تيار العقل وتيار النقل؟ أما أن يوجد عند آحاد العلماء في القديم أو الحديث، فذلك لا يرقى ليمثل اتجاهين متنافرين متناحرين، كما هذه الصورة عنهما الكاتب. أجل إن طوفاناً من التقليد غشى العقل المسلم ردحاً من الزمن وما تزال آثاره تفعل فعلها حتى اليوم، ولهذا فمما يجدر التأكيد عليه هنا أن ليس في عدم الموافقة على هذا التصنيف ونتائجه ما يدفع للذود عن جمود أصاب الفكر الإسلامي بعامة، ولا تبريراً للتقليد الذي وقع في إساره جمهور كبير من الفقهاء والمحدثين، فقاد إلى تدهور مريع في شتى الجوانب، حتى أطلق على فترة غير قصيرة من تاريخنا سمة الانحطاط الحضاري والثقافي، وليس في هذا الوصف مخالفة أو تجاوز مبالغ فيه، ولكن الإصرار على تصوير مسألة العقل والنقل في تاريخنا بتلك الثنائية العقيمة كما لو كان المخرج الوحيد أمام أزمة العقل المسلم المعاصر هو الانحياز بالكامل لتيار (العقل) في مقابل رفض النقل وإقصاء أدواره المعرفية والسلوكية الإصرار على ذلك هو المرفوض. ويعلم الدارسون للفكر الإسلامي أن ثمة مناطق فيه لا يطالها العقل مباشرة إلا عن طريق الاستدلال النقلي، وذلك كما في تفصيلات العقيدة، مثل أركان الإيمان الستة المعلومة، والتي سبق الإشارة إليها عند الحديث عن ميدان المعرفة. وذلك ما يعرف بعالم الغيب، وما تطلق عليه هذه الدراسة بـ(ميدان المعرفة في عالم الغيب. وإلى هذا أشار ابن تيمية بقوله: (فما أخبرت به الرسل من تفاصيل اليوم الآخر، وأُمرت به تفاصيل الشرائع لا يعلمه الناس بعقولهم، كما أن ما أخبرت به الرسل من تفصيل أسماء الله
And in a later point in his study, it is considered that conflict occurred in Islamic thought upon the encounter of the Islamic mind with the Greek mind... this one with its beliefs and unseen matters, and that one with its rationalism and objectivity... it may be a heavy thing for our hearts to admit that the conservative forces in Arab-Islamic educational thought succeeded, after the coup of al-Mutawakkil and the issuance of the Qadiri creed in 413 AH, in retreating from the era of al-Ma'mun and defeating reason, demonstrative reason; that is what was intended. Such talk represents strong evidence of what was mentioned earlier of the manifestations of civilizational alienation in the contemporary Muslim mind, such that it came to conceptualize the problem of the sources of knowledge and its methods in this manner. So is it taken for granted that the traditionalists definitively settled the position on the source of knowledge and what pertains to it merely because they believed in the unseen and their restriction of education to the religious goal, by which the absent is measured by the present... etc. Presenting the subject in this manner is a disgraceful oversimplification of the truth of the matter, for the division in this way (traditionalists) and (rationalists) as if they are two opposing, contradictory currents with no meeting or agreement does not represent objective reality. Rather, it confirms falling into the trap of civilizational alienation, contrary to historical reality. Has any one of us heard of a battle or battles of this magnitude between the current of reason and the current of transmission? As for it existing among some scholars of the past or present, that does not rise to represent two mutually hostile and warring trends, as this image drawn by the author. Yes, a flood of imitation (taqlid) overtook the Muslim mind for a period of time, and its effects are still acting until today, and for this reason, it is worth emphasizing here that disagreeing with this classification and its results does not entail defending stagnation that afflicted Islamic thought in general, nor an apology for the imitation that a large number of jurists and hadith scholars fell into, which led to a terrible decline in various aspects, such that a not-short period of our history was characterized as civilizational and cultural decline. And there is no violation or exaggeration in this description, but insisting on depicting the issue of reason and transmission in our history with that sterile dichotomy as if the only way out of the contemporary Muslim mind's crisis is to fully side with the current of (reason) in opposition to rejecting transmission and excluding its epistemological and behavioral roles — insisting on that is what is rejected. And students of Islamic thought know that there are areas in it that reason does not reach directly except through transmitted inference, such as in the details of creed, like the well-known six pillars of faith, which were previously referenced when discussing the field of knowledge. That is what is known as the world of the unseen, and what this study calls (the field of knowledge in the world of the unseen). And Ibn Taymiyya pointed to this with his saying: 'What the messengers informed of the details of the Last Day, and the details of the laws they commanded, people do not know by their minds, just as what the messengers informed of the detailed names of Allah...'
Source pages p. 331

Commentary
This passage is a critical response to a reductive binary categorization of Islamic intellectual history into 'naqliyyun' (traditionalists) and 'aqliyyun' (rationalists). The author, a modern scholar, argues that this dichotomy is a product of 'istilab hadari' (civilizational alienation) and does not reflect historical reality. He begins by referencing a conflict between Islamic and Greek thought, noting that conservative forces after al-Mutawakkil's coup defeated demonstrative reason. He then critiques the contemporary presentation of the issue, stating that dividing scholars into these two opposing camps is a distortion. He acknowledges that there was a period of taqlid (imitation) and decline, but insists that rejecting the classification and its conclusions does not mean defending that stagnation. Instead, the insistence on a binary choice — siding entirely with reason and rejecting transmission — is what is wrong. He then affirms that there are domains of knowledge, like the details of the unseen (ghayb), that reason cannot access directly without transmitted evidence. He cites Ibn Taymiyya to support this, quoting that the details of the afterlife and religious laws are not known by reason alone. The passage thus refines the common misunderstanding that Islamic thought is neatly split into rationalist and traditionalist camps, emphasizing the complementary roles of reason and revelation.

نقليون / عقليون
تقليد
غيب

The false dichotomy between 'aqli' and 'naqli' obscures the complementary roles of reason and revelation in Islamic thought, a nuance recognized by classical scholars like Ibn Taymiyya.

Critique of the Reason-Revelation Dichotomy
Author critiques the sterile reason-revelation dichotomy and proposes complementarity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct the author's argument against the sterile dichotomy between reason and transmission, and state the proper Islamic position on their relationship.

Core Idea
Reason and revelation are complementary; reason is the guide of revelation, and revelation completes reason.

This passage tackles a persistent problem in Islamic thought: the false opposition between reason and transmitted knowledge. The author argues that this dichotomy is not only unproductive but also leads to intellectual stagnation. Instead, he presents a nuanced view where reason serves as the guide and tool for understanding revelation, while revelation provides access to realms beyond reason's direct reach, such as the unseen.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's diagnosis of the problem
Read the first paragraph and note how the author describes the effects of taqlid (blind imitation) and the 'sterile dichotomy' between reason and transmission. What is he rejecting?
The author rejects the idea that the only solution to the crisis is to side completely with reason against transmission.
2
Extract the areas beyond reason
In the second paragraph, the author specifies domains where reason alone is insufficient. Identify these domains and the method required to access them.
The details of creed (e.g., pillars of faith) and the unseen require transmitted inference, not direct reason.
3
Analyze the Ibn Taymiyya quote
Read the quote from Ibn Taymiyya. What does it say about the role of reason regarding the details of the Last Day, laws, and divine attributes?
Ibn Taymiyya distinguishes between general understanding (which reason can grasp) and specific details (which require revelation).
4
Synthesize the complementary relationship
In the final paragraph, the author describes reason as 'guide of revelation' and revelation as granting 'infallible values'. Explain how this resolves the false dichotomy.
Reason is essential for understanding and transmitting revelation, but revelation provides content that reason cannot generate.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أجل إن طوفاناً من التقليد غشى العقل المسلم ردحاً من الزمن وما تزال آثاره تفعل فعلها حتى اليوم، ولهذا فمما يجدر التأكيد عليه هنا أن ليس في عدم الموافقة على هذا التصنيف ونتائجه ما يدفع للذود عن جمود أصاب الفكر الإسلامي بعامة، ولا تبريراً للتقليد الذي وقع في إساره جمهور كبير من الفقهاء والمحدثين، فقاد إلى تدهور مريع في شتى الجوانب، حتى أطلق على فترة غير قصيرة من تاريخنا سمة الانحطاط الحضاري والثقافي)، وليس في هذا الوصف مخالفة أو تجاوز مبالغ فيه، ولكن الإصرار على تصوير مسألة العقل والنقل في تاريخنا بتلك الثنائية العقيمة كما لو كان المخرج الوحيد أمام أزمة العقل المسلم المعاصر هو الانحياز بالكامل لتيار (العقل) في مقابل رفض النقل وإقصاء أدواره المعرفية والسلوكية الإصرار على ذلك هو المرفوض.

ويعلم الدارسون للفكر الإسلامي أن ثمة مناطق فيه لا يطالها العقل مباشرة إلا عن طريق الاستدلال النقلي، وذلك كما في تفصيلات العقيدة، مثل أركان الإيمان الستة المعلومة، والتي سبق الإشارة إليها عند الحديث عن ميدان المعرفة. وذلك ما يعرف بعالم الغيب، وما تطلق عليه هذه الدراسة بـ(ميدان المعرفة في عالم الغيب). وإلى هذا أشار ابن تيمية بقوله:

(فما أخبرت به الرسل من تفاصيل اليوم الآخر، وأُمرت به تفاصيل الشرائع لا يعلمه الناس بعقولهم، كما أن ما أخبرت به الرسل من تفصيل أسماء الله وصفاته لا يعلمه الناس بعقولهم وإن كانوا قد يعلمون بعقولهم محمل ذلك) (1).

وحسبنا أن نؤكد أن العقل في الإسلام دليل الوحي، ووسيلة فهمه ونقله ومحل تكليفه وأن الوحي من بعض الوجوه يمكن أن يعتبر أحد مدارج العقل ومعارفه) (2). كما أن العقل في الإسلام سند الحقيقة، وأن الوحي هو الإطار المرجعي الذي يمنح العقل القيم المعصومة) (3).
Yes, indeed a flood of imitation overwhelmed the Muslim mind for a long period, and its effects continue to have their impact until today. Hence, it is worth emphasizing here that disagreement with this classification and its results does not justify defending a rigidity that afflicted Islamic thought in general, nor does it justify the imitation within which a large majority of jurists and hadith scholars fell, leading to a terrible deterioration in various aspects, so that a non-short period of our history was labeled with the characteristic of civilizational and cultural decline. And there is no violation or exaggeration in this description, but the insistence on portraying the issue of reason and transmission in our history with that sterile dichotomy, as if the only way out of the crisis of the contemporary Muslim mind is to completely side with the trend of (reason) in opposition to rejecting transmission and excluding its epistemological and behavioral roles—that insistence is rejected.

The scholars of Islamic thought know that there are areas in it that reason does not directly reach except through transmitted inference, such as in the details of creed, like the well-known six pillars of faith, which were previously referred to when discussing the field of knowledge. That is what is known as the realm of the unseen, and this study calls it the 'field of knowledge in the realm of the unseen.' And Ibn Taymiyya referred to this by saying:

'Whatever the messengers informed about the details of the Last Day, and the details of the laws that they commanded, people do not know them by their reason, just as what the messengers informed about the details of Allah's names and attributes, people do not know them by their reason, even though they may know by their reason the bearing (i.e., the general meaning) of that' (1).

It suffices us to affirm that reason in Islam is the guide of revelation, the means of understanding it, transmitting it, and the locus of its obligation, and that revelation from some perspectives can be considered one of the ranks of reason and its cognitions (2). Also, reason in Islam is the support of truth, and revelation is the reference framework that grants reason infallible values (3).
Source pages p. 332

Commentary
This passage is a critical analysis of the dichotomy between reason and transmitted knowledge in Islamic history. The author begins by condemning the widespread phenomenon of blind imitation (taqlid) that has afflicted Muslim thought, leading to decline. However, he stresses that disagreement with a particular classification does not justify rigidity or the rejection of reason. He then attacks the simplistic binary opposition between 'aql and naql, arguing that it is sterile and unproductive. He points out that there are areas of knowledge, particularly details of creed and the unseen, that are not accessible to unaided reason but require transmitted evidence. He cites Ibn Taymiyya to support this view. Yet, he asserts that reason in Islam serves as the guide for revelation, the means of understanding it, and that revelation can be seen as a mode of reason. Thus, reason and revelation are complementary, not opposed.

النقل

التقليد

A) Reason is independent of revelation and can replace it.

Key Takeaway
The reason-revelation dichotomy is a false dilemma; in Islam, reason serves as the guide and tool for revelation, while revelation provides knowledge of the unseen and infallible values.

Rejecting the Religious-Secular Education Dichotomy
Author argues against religious-secular education dichotomy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct the author's argument against the religious-secular education split and show how the comprehensive definition of worship ('ibada) supports it.

Core Idea
Islamic education is holistic because worship ('ibada) encompasses all actions pleasing to God.

In many modern discussions, education is divided into religious and secular. But does this split hold within the Islamic worldview? The author here argues that it does not, because the very concept of worship in Islam is all-encompassing. Let's examine how he uses this definition to reject the dichotomy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's main claim
Read the passage and find where the author explicitly rejects the split between religious and secular education. Look for phrases like 'انشطاراً بين الدين والدنيا'.
The author calls it a 'crossroads' (مفترق الطريق) with no benefit.
2
Extract the definition of worship ('ibada)
Find the definition of worship provided in the passage. It is given in parentheses with a reference. Write it down: 'اسم جامع لكل ما يحبه الله ويرضاه من الأقوال والأعمال الباطنة والظاهرة'.
This definition is attributed to Ibn Taymiyya and is broader than just rituals.
3
Connect the definition to education
Explain how this broad definition of worship implies that all education, including subjects like medicine or engineering, can be acts of worship if done with the right intention within Islam's comprehensive framework.
The author says education has 'أبعاد شمولية' (comprehensive dimensions).
4
Apply the concept to a modern example
Choose a subject often called 'secular', like economics. Using the author's logic, show how studying economics can be an act of worship if pursued with the intention of benefiting society in a way pleasing to God.
This demonstrates the practical implication of rejecting the split.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما تقييدهم للتعليم بالهدف الديني فلا إشكال في ذلك إذا ما أخذنا في الاعتبار الإطار الموضوعي لذلك القول زماناً ومكاناً، ثم إذا ما اتفقنا على مرجعية (الإسلام) الكلية وانطلقنا في فهم حركة الفرد والمجتمع من منطلق أن العبادة اسم جامع لكل ما يحبه الله ويرضاه من الأقوال والأعمال الباطنة والظاهرة (4) . وأن التربية عملية ذات أبعاد شمولية جميعها مما حث الإسلام على رعايتها وله فيها وجهة وموقف في إطار تصوره الشامل للإنسان والكون والحياة. وحينئذ فإن الهدف الديني يمكن أن يكون هدفاً عاماً تنضوي تحته جملة الأهداف الفرعية أو الخاصة جميعاً. أما حين نتصور أن ثمة انشطاراً بين الدين والدنيا، أو أن ثمة تعليماً دينياً وآخر علمانياً فذلك مفترق الطريق، ولا ثمرة ساعتئذ من النقاش، إذ إن الحكم على الشيء فرع عن تصوره.

وأعجب لقول الكاتب في السياق المقابل ربط العقلانيون الغاية من العلم والتعلم بالدين كما فعل أهل النقل ولكن على نحو آخر). أو في ذلك حقاً ما يستدعي الاستنكار والعجب... أو يشترط في كل صاحب عقل أن يُطلق
As for their restriction of education to the religious goal, there is no problem with that if we take into consideration the objective context of that statement in time and place, and then if we agree on the comprehensive reference of (Islam) and proceed in understanding the movement of the individual and society from the premise that worship is a comprehensive name for everything that Allah loves and is pleased with from inward and outward sayings and deeds (4). And that education is a process with comprehensive dimensions, all of which Islam has urged to care for and has a perspective and position on within its comprehensive conception of man, the universe, and life. Then the religious goal can be a general goal under which all subsidiary or specific goals are subsumed. But when we imagine that there is a split between religion and this world, or that there is religious education and secular education, that is the crossroads, and there is no benefit then from discussion, for the judgment on a thing is a branch of its conception.

And I am amazed at the statement of the writer in the opposite context: 'The rationalists linked the purpose of knowledge and learning to religion, just as the people of transmission did, but in another way.' Is there really in that what warrants disapproval and amazement... or does it require every person of reason to release...
Source pages p. 333

Commentary
This passage addresses the issue of education, specifically the claim that Islamic education restricts learning to religious goals. The author argues that this is acceptable within a proper understanding of Islam's comprehensive framework. He defines worship ('ibada) broadly to include all actions pleasing to God, and emphasizes that education is holistic. The religious goal is overarching, not exclusive. He then rejects the dichotomy between religious and secular education, stating that it leads to a dead end. Finally, he criticizes a writer who claims that rationalists also linked learning to religion, implying that this is not objectionable but perhaps the rationalists did it differently.

Key Takeaway
Islamic education is holistic; the religious goal encompasses all subsidiary goals because worship includes all actions pleasing to God.

Definition of Intuition (al-Hads) and Its Philosophical Shift
Author defines intuition linguistically and philosophically as a secondary knowledge source.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the linguistic and philosophical definitions of al-hads and evaluate the author's defense of the technical usage.

Core Idea
Intuition: from guesswork to direct insight, yet secondary to revelation and reason.

In this passage, the author defines 'al-hads' (intuition) in both its linguistic and philosophical senses. Understanding this shift is crucial because intuition is often misunderstood as a primary source of knowledge. The author not only clarifies the definitions but also defends the philosophical usage against literalist objections. By studying this lesson, you will learn how to distinguish between linguistic and technical meanings and appreciate the principle that technical terms evolve from language but need not be identical to it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic definition
Look at the first sentence. Al-hads in Arabic means conjecture, guesswork, and direct perception. Note also the verbal forms given.
The linguistic meaning is the starting point for understanding the term.
2
Extract the philosophical definitions
The author gives multiple philosophical meanings: direct perception of the object of thinking, sudden inspiration without induction/deduction, and quick grasp of truth without external sense or reasoning. List them.
These definitions share the idea of immediacy and lack of intermediary.
3
Analyze al-Fakhr al-Razi's definition
Al-Razi defines hads as an intermediary between the two ends of the unknown and the soul's preparedness to find that intermediary. This relates to finding the middle term in a syllogism.
This definition connects intuition to logical reasoning.
4
Understand the objection and response
A researcher objects that the philosophical meaning (speed of thought) is not linguistically valid. The author counters that technical terms rely on the essence of linguistic meaning, not literal wording.
The key evidence from language is that 'direct perception' is a valid linguistic sense.
5
Evaluate the author's justification
Does the author successfully justify the philosophical usage? Assess whether the linguistic basis (direct perception) adequately supports the philosophical meaning (immediate knowledge).
Consider that technical terminology often extends core meanings.

تعريف الحدس
الحدس لغة: الظن والتخمين وبابه ،ضرب يقال هو يحدس أي يقول شيئا برأيه(١). والجنس إدراك الشيء إدراكًا مباشراً، وتحدس الأخبار تحسسها (٢).
وأما المعنى الفلسفي للحدس فيأتي بمعنى: الإدراك المباشر لموضوع التفكين)(۱) . وبمعنى: «اطلاع النفس المباشر على ما يمثله لها الحس الظاهر، أو الحس الباطن من صور حسيّة أو نفسية، أو على كشف الذهن عن بعض الحقائق بوحي مفاجئ لا على سبيل الاستقراء أو الاستنتاج، ولكن على سبيل المشاهدة، التي ينبلج فيها الحق انبلاجاً)) (۳). كما يأتي الحدس بمعنى: «الإدراك السريع المفاجئ للموقف أو الحقيقة، دون حاجة إلى حس خارجي، أو استدلال (٣) . وعرفه الفخر الرازي (ت: ٦٠٤ هـ ) بأنه عبارة عن متوسط بين طرفي المجهول، واستعداد النفس لوجدان ذلك المتوسط هو الحنس ) وتطور مفهوم الحدس حتى غدا مذهباً في المعرفة يعرف بالمذهب الحدسي .(Intuitionism)
ويشار إلى أن هنري برجسون (Henri Bergson) الفيلسوف الفرنسي (ت: ١٩٤١م) يَعدُّ هذا المذهب السبيل الوحيد لمعرفة المطلق). وأحياناً يطلق على المذهب الذي يقول باعتماد المعرفة على الحدس (الحدسية)(1).
ويستدرك أحد الباحثين على استعمال الفلاسفة للحنس بمعنى سرعة الانتقال والفهم والاستنتاج بأنه ليس استعمالاً جاءت به اللغة، ولا أقر في معاجمها (۳). وكأنه يعني حرفية المعنى، ولكن من المعلوم بأن المعنى الاصطلاحي لا يلتزم حرفية المعنى اللغوي، وإنما يعتمد على جوهره لتجسير المعنيين. وإذا كانت اللغة قد قالت بأن من معاني الحدس إدراك الشيء إدراكاً مباشراً فإن ذلك مستند قوي للاصطلاح الفلسفي القائل بسرعة الانتقال والفهم والاستنتاج.
Definition of intuition: Intuition linguistically: conjecture and guesswork, its paradigm (بابه ضرب), one says 'he intuits' meaning he says something by his opinion. And directly perceiving something, 'tahaddus al-akhbar' means investigating them. As for the philosophical meaning of intuition, it comes to mean: direct perception of the object of thinking. And it means: the soul's direct awareness of what is represented to it by the external sense or the internal sense of sensory or psychological images, or the mind's uncovering of some truths by sudden inspiration not through induction or deduction, but through observation in which truth shines forth. And also intuition comes to mean: quick sudden perception of the situation or truth, without need for external sense or reasoning. Al-Fakhr al-Razi (d. 604 AH) defined it as: an intermediary between the two ends of the unknown, and the soul's preparedness to find that intermediary is intuition. The concept of intuition developed until it became a school in knowledge known as Intuitionism. It is pointed out that Henri Bergson, the French philosopher (d. 1941 CE), considers this school as the only way to know the absolute. Sometimes it is called the school that holds to reliance on intuition for knowledge (al-hadsiyya). One researcher objects to the philosophers' use of intuition to mean speed of transition and understanding and deduction, saying it is not a usage found in language nor approved in its dictionaries. As if he means literalness of meaning, but it is known that the technical meaning does not adhere to the literal linguistic meaning, rather it relies on its essence to bridge the two meanings. And if the language said that among the meanings of intuition is direct perception of something, then that is a strong basis for the philosophical term meaning speed of transition and understanding and deduction.
Source pages p. 336

Commentary
This passage is a definitional exposition of the concept of 'al-hads' (intuition) as a secondary source of knowledge in Islamic epistemology. The author begins by presenting the linguistic definition of hads: it means conjecture, guesswork, or direct perception. This is grounded in the Arabic language, as cited from lexical works. Then the author moves to the philosophical meaning, which is distinct but rooted in the linguistic sense. He gives multiple definitions: direct perception, sudden inspiration without induction or deduction, and quick grasp of truth without external sense or reasoning. He quotes al-Fakhr al-Razi, who defines intuition as an intermediary between the two extremes of the unknown (i.e., a middle term in a syllogism) and the soul's readiness to find it. The author notes that the concept evolved into a full epistemological school (Intuitionism), citing Henri Bergson as a proponent. Finally, the author addresses a criticism that the philosophical use of hads (as speed of thought) is not linguistically valid. He rejects the literalist objection by arguing that technical terms need not exactly match their linguistic origins; the core meaning of 'direct perception' in language supports the philosophical usage. Throughout, the passage emphasizes that while intuition is recognized, it remains a secondary source compared to revelation, reason, and sense — as established earlier in the chapter. The commentary should note that the author's purpose is to define and validate the concept without elevating it above primary sources.

The philosophical meaning of al-hads as intuitive knowledge is legitimate because it is rooted in the linguistic sense of direct perception, but it remains a secondary source dependent on primary sources like revelation and reason.

The Role and Limits of Intuition in Islamic Epistemology
Author defines intuition and sets conditions for its validity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate when intuition is a valid source of knowledge according to Islamic epistemology.

Core Idea
Intuition is valid only when it does not contradict reason, revelation, or sense.

In this passage, the author discusses intuition (al-hads) as a subordinate source of knowledge. He defines it, gives examples from science, and clarifies that while intuition can be valuable, it must be checked against the primary sources. This lesson will help you distinguish between valid intuition and superstitious thinking.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of intuition
Read the passage and extract the author's description of intuition as sudden insights after deep contemplation.
2
Analyze the Otto Loewi example
Consider how his dream-inspired idea fits the definition. Was it valid? Why did it succeed?
Loewi trusted his intuition because it did not conflict with his scientific knowledge.
3
Determine the condition for rejection
Find where the author says intuition becomes superstitious. What is the condition?
The condition is conflict with reliable sources like reason.
4
Identify the permissible scope
When does the author consider intuition valid as a source? Look for the phrase 'fields in which none of revelation, sense, or reason operate'.
5
Summarize the epistemological status
Synthesize: intuition is subordinate and conditional; it must agree with primary sources.
This aligns with Islamic epistemology's hierarchy of sources.

المعلومات الناقصة. ومن هنا فإن القادرين على الحدس هم وحدهم المخترعون والمبتكرون في مختلف ميادين العلم والفن والأدب (١) ، وإن كانت أبرز مظاهر الحدس تبلوراً في الأحكام الجمالية (٢) . وذلك بقطع النظر عن مدى تدين الحدسيين، فثمة علماء ومفكرون وأدباء خبروا تلك الطريقة بعد تأمل عميق وجدوا بعده بصائر فجائية أو لحظات إلهام غامرة (٣). ومن ذلك ما يقصه (أوتولوي) الحاصل على جائزة نوبل في الفسيولوجيا والطب سنة (١٩٢٦م)، حين خطرت له فكرة تجريبية أثناء نومه وكانت أساساً في تكوين النظرية الكيميائية الخاصة بنقل التيار العصبي، وبها حصل على الجائزة، وفي هذا يقول: إن قصة هذا الاكتشاف تظهر أن إحدى الأفكار قد تنام عشرات السنين في العقل اللاشعوري، ثم تعود فجأة، وأكثر من هذا، فإنها تشير إلى أننا ينبغي أن أحيانًا في الحدس الفجائي دون تشكك كثيراً جداً. فلأني كنت تناولته بعناية في أثناء النهار، كنت بلا شك قد أغضيت هذا النوع من التجارب الذي اضطلعت به وكان من حسن الحظ أنه في لحظة الحس الباطني أنني لم أفكر بل أقدمت على العمل))(٤). نثق واكتشاف (أوتولوي) هذا يردّ على الذين قصروا عمل الحدس في مجالات الأعمال الفنية والأدبية الفن الشعر - (الأدب لأن هذه المجالات - في نظرهم مما يتطلب هذا المصدر، في حين يعجز العقل الدقيق عن الأخذ بأيدينا إليها. وبناء على ذلك فإن الحدس لا يصلح مرشداً لنا في ميدان المعرفة ذاتها، حتى أن أصحاب المذهب الحدسي يتركون قدرة العقل، أو يجعلون له مكانة ثانوية فقط، وهذا ما يمثل عقبة أمام التفكير العلمي(٥). والواقع أن تقييدهم هذا لا يقلل من أهمية الحدس في عملية المعرفة، كما لا يشكك في سلامة التفكير الحدسي، إلا حينما يقف عقبة – بالفعل – أمـام التفكير العلمي، ومصادماً للمصادر والطرائق المعتبرة كالعقل مثلاً، وفي هذه الحال يستحيل الحدس إلى ضرب من التفكير الخرافي المرفوض. أما فيما عدا هذه الحال فإني لا أذهب بعيداً إذا ما اعتبرته عاماً صالحاً لكل الميادين التي لا يعمل فيها أي من الوحي أو الحس أو العقل، نتيجة لقلة المعلومات المتاحة لنا فيها، إذ الحدس - في هذه الحال - إنما يستمد صدق استنتاجه بدعم منها حين يوافقها، ولا يأتي بأحكام واستنتاجات تتصادم مع منطقها.
Incomplete information. Hence, those capable of intuition are the inventors and innovators in various fields of science, art, and literature (1), although the most prominent manifestations of intuition crystallize in aesthetic judgments (2). This is regardless of the religiosity of intuitive persons; there are scientists, thinkers, and writers who experienced that method after deep contemplation and afterward found sudden insights or overwhelming moments of inspiration (3). Among that is what Otto Loewi, Nobel Prize laureate in physiology and medicine in 1926, recounts when an experimental idea occurred to him during his sleep and was the basis for forming the chemical theory of nerve impulse transmission, and with it he won the prize. In this regard, he says: 'The story of this discovery shows that an idea may sleep for decades in the subconscious mind, then suddenly return, and more than that, it indicates that we should sometimes trust sudden intuition without much doubt. Because if I had handled it carefully during the day, I would undoubtedly have dismissed this type of experiment I undertook. It was fortunate that in the moment of inner sense I did not think but proceeded to work.' (4). We trust. And this discovery of Otto Loewi refutes those who limited the work of intuition to the fields of artistic and literary works - art, poetry, literature - because these fields in their view require this source, while the precise mind is incapable of guiding us to them. Accordingly, intuition is not suitable as a guide for us in the field of knowledge itself, such that the adherents of the intuitive school abandon the power of reason, or give it only a secondary status, and this represents an obstacle to scientific thinking (5). In reality, this restriction of theirs does not diminish the importance of intuition in the process of knowledge, nor does it cast doubt on the soundness of intuitive thinking, except when it actually stands as an obstacle to scientific thinking and conflicts with reliable sources and methods such as reason. In this case, intuition turns into a type of rejected superstitious thinking. Apart from this case, I am not going too far if I consider it a general factor valid for all fields in which none of revelation, sense, or reason operate, due to the scarcity of information available to us in them. For intuition, in this case, derives the truth of its conclusion from their support when it agrees with them, and it does not bring judgments and conclusions that conflict with their logic.

Commentary
This passage defines intuition (الحدس) as a subordinate source of knowledge, starting by stating that those capable of intuition are the inventors and innovators in science, art, and literature. The author notes that intuition is most evident in aesthetic judgments. Examples follow, such as the story of Otto Loewi, who had an experimental idea during sleep that led to a Nobel Prize-winning discovery. The author then refutes the view that intuition is limited to artistic fields, arguing that intuition is not a reliable guide in knowledge when it conflicts with reason. However, the author clarifies that intuition is not inherently problematic; it becomes superstitious only when it contradicts reliable sources like reason. Otherwise, intuition can be valid in fields where revelation, sense, or reason are insufficient due to lack of information. The author emphasizes that intuition derives its truth from agreement with these sources and does not produce judgments that conflict with their logic.

Six Characteristics of Intuition in a 1966 Experiment
Author lists six characteristics of intuitive thinking based on a 1966 study.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the six characteristics of intuition (al-hads) from the 1966 psychological experiment and compare them to the classical Islamic epistemological concept of hads.

Core Idea
Modern psychology and Islamic philosophy both study 'hads'—but from different angles.

In this lesson, we examine a 1966 psychological experiment that systematically identifies six characteristics of intuitive thinking (al-hads). As we explore these traits, we will compare them to the classical Islamic understanding of hads as a source of knowledge. This exercise sharpens our ability to distinguish empirical findings from philosophical definitions.

Guided Path
1
Locate each characteristic in the Arabic text
Read the six numbered points in the Arabic passage. Note the key Arabic terms: الانبساط, سرعة الأداء, etc. Identify what trait each point describes.
2
Connect each characteristic to the Islamic term 'al-hads'
For each trait, ask: Is this something that classical Muslims (like Ibn Sina or Ghazali) would include in their concept of hads? For example, extroversion is not part of the classical definition, but speed of insight might be.
3
Identify characteristics that seem incompatible with Islamic epistemology
Consider trait 4: animism. How does this relate to tawheed? Note to yourself why this might clash.
4
Summarize: which characteristics are universal, and which are culture-bound?
Based on your analysis, decide which of the six likely apply to hads in any context, and which might be specific to modern Western subjects.

خصائص الحدس
قام سيد أحمد عثمان سنة (١٩٦٦م) بإجراء تجربة نفسية حول التفكير الحدسي (Intuitive Thinking) وتوصل إلى ما يلي:
۱ تومئ نتائج البحث بأن الحدس أقرب إلى سمة الانبساط في الشخصية منه إلى الانطواء.
۲ - سرعة الأداء لا المباشرة (Immedicay).
- لا يرتبط الحدس بسلوك المسايرة أو المعايير الاجتماعية.
- ثمة علاقة بين الحدس والنزعة الإحيائية (animism)(١).
ء - التفكير الحدسي أقرب إلى النزعة التفاؤلية منه إلى التشاؤمية.
٦ - عملية الحدس تكاملية مع بقية أنواع التفكير الأخرى كالعلاقة والمرونة والاستدلال.
(١) الإحيائية (animism) أو المذهب الحيوي أو الأرواحية القول بأن لكل ما في الكون روحا أو نفساً)). (محمد علي الخولي، قاموس التربية، ٢٢).
Characteristics of Intuition
Sayed Ahmed Othman in 1966 conducted a psychological experiment on intuitive thinking and arrived at the following:
1. The results of the research indicate that intuition is closer to the extroversion trait in personality than to introversion.
2. Speed of performance, not immediacy.
3. Intuition is not related to compliance behavior or social norms.
4. There is a relationship between intuition and animism (1).
5. Intuitive thinking is closer to optimism than to pessimism.
6. The process of intuition is integrative with other types of thinking such as relationship, flexibility, and inference.
(1) Animism: the doctrine that everything in the universe has a spirit or soul. (Muhammad Ali al-Khouli, Dictionary of Education, p. 22).
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage presents the results of a psychological experiment by Sayed Ahmed Othman in 1966 on intuitive thinking. It enumerates six characteristics: first, intuition is associated with extroversion rather than introversion. Second, it involves speed of performance but not necessarily immediacy (the term 'Immedicay' is likely a typo for 'Immediacy'). Third, intuition is independent of conformity to social norms. Fourth, there is a link between intuition and animism, the belief that everything has a spirit. Fifth, intuitive thinking tends towards optimism rather than pessimism. Sixth, intuition integrates with other thinking types such as relationship, flexibility, and inference. These characteristics paint intuition as a personality-linked, rapid, and holistic cognitive process.

الانبساط
الإحيائية

Conditions for Valid Intuition in Islam
Author defines the scope of valid intuition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions under which intuition is considered a valid secondary source of knowledge in the Islamic epistemological framework.

Core Idea
Intuition is valid only when it aligns with revelation, sense, and reason.

Intuition is often misunderstood as mere guesswork, but in Islamic epistemology it has a defined role as a secondary source. This lesson unpacks the author's key conditions: intuition is acceptable when it does not contradict revelation, sensory evidence, or rational inference. Understanding these boundaries helps distinguish reliable intuition from superstitious thinking.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's main claim about intuition
Read the first paragraph and note the author's assertion that intuition is generally valid except when it obstructs scientific thinking or conflicts with reliable sources like reason.
2
Extract the three primary sources that validate intuition
The author mentions revelation (al-wahy), sense (al-hiss), and reason (al-‘aql). Intuition is valid when it does not contradict these and even derives support from them when in agreement.
These are the three primary sources in Islamic epistemology.
3
Determine when intuition becomes invalid
When intuition contradicts these sources, it turns into superstitious thinking (tafkir khurafi). This is the key boundary condition.
4
Apply the condition to a scenario
Consider an intuitive feeling about a religious ruling. If it contradicts a clear Quranic verse, it is invalid. If it aligns, it may be acceptable in areas where revelation is silent.
This mirrors the principle of istihsan in usul al-fiqh.

الباب الثالث: الفصل الرابع - المصادر التبعية
والواقع أن تقييدهم هذا لا يقلل من أهمية الحدس في عملية المعرفة، كما لا يشكك في سلامة التفكير الحدسي، إلا حينما يقف عقبة – بالفعل – أمام التفكير العلمي، ومصادماً للمصادر والطرائق المعتبرة كالعقل مثلاً، وفي هذه الحال يستحيل الحدس إلى ضرب من التفكير الخرافي المرفوض. أما فيما عدا هذه الحال فإني لا أذهب بعيداً إذا ما اعتبرته عاماً صالحاً لكل الميادين التي لا يعمل فيها أي من الوحي أو الحس أو العقل، نتيجة لقلة المعلومات المتاحة لنا فيها، إذ الحدس - في هذه الحال - إنما يستمد صدق استنتاجه بدعم منها حين يوافقها، ولا يأتي بأحكام واستنتاجات تتصادم مع منطقها.
خصائص الحدس
قام سيد أحمد عثمان سنة (١٩٦٦م) بإجراء تجربة نفسية حول التفكير الحدسي (Intuitive Thinking) وتوصل إلى ما يلي:
۱ تومئ نتائج البحث بأن الحدس أقرب إلى سمة الانبساط في الشخصية منه إلى الانطواء.
۲ - سرعة الأداء لا المباشرة (Immedicay).
- لا يرتبط الحدس بسلوك المسايرة أو المعايير الاجتماعية.
- ثمة علاقة بين الحدس والنزعة الإحيائية (animism).
ء - التفكير الحدسي أقرب إلى النزعة التفاؤلية منه إلى التشاؤمية. ٦ - عملية الحدس تكاملية مع بقية أنواع التفكير الأخرى كالعلاقة والمرونة والاستدلال.
لا يرتبط الحدس بالتخمين المحض Wild Guess أي إن المفهوم السائد عن الحدس بمعنى التخمين ليس له أساس علمي.
۸ - مجموعة الأفراد ذوو التفكير الحدسي (Intuitive Thinking) أكثر سيطرة واتزانا انفعاليا ومسؤولية.
وأراد بعض الباحثين تلخيص تلك السمات فأوجزها في نقاط ثلاث هي:
١- معرفة مباشرة لا تحتاج إلى وسائط، ولا تدرّج فيها.
٢- الانتقال المباشر إلى لب الموضوع المعروف بدلا تقديمه أوصافاً من خارجية أو سطحية للموضوع، أو يقتصر على معرفته من خلال مقارنته بغيره.
٣- معرفة فردية لا تنتقل إلى الآخرين ولا يمكن تلقينها أو تعميمها.
موقف القرآن من الحدس
قبل المبادرة إلى تسجيل ما يبدو أنه موقف للقرآن من التفكير الحدسي بوصفه مصدراً في الحصول على المعرفة أخال أنه من غير الموضوعية إغفال مدى التأثير الكبير لـ (هنري برجسون) الذي يعدّ مؤسساً لهذا الاتجاه في العصر الحاضر. مما جرَّ كثيراً من الباحثين المعاصرين لتحديد موقفهم من الحدس في ضوء رؤية برجسون.
والحق أنه أياً ما كان من اهتمام متميّز لهنري برجسون بالحدس حتى أضحى صاحب نظرية قمينة بالدراسة؛ فإن ذلك لا يجعل من دراسته معياراً عاماً مطّرداً، إذ إن أكبر عامل نقد موضوعي يوجه إلى نظريته تلك – من زاوية التصور الإسلامي - قيامها بعيداً عن توجيهات الوحي واستهداءاته.
Chapter Three: Section Four - Secondary Sources. In reality, their restriction does not diminish the importance of intuition in the process of knowledge, nor does it doubt the soundness of intuitive thinking, except when it actually becomes an obstacle to scientific thinking and conflicts with reliable sources and methods such as reason, in which case intuition turns into a type of rejected superstitious thinking. Aside from this case, I am not going too far if I consider it generally valid for all fields in which none of revelation, sense, or reason operate, due to the scarcity of information available to us in them, since intuition in this case derives the truth of its inference from support by them when it agrees with them, and it does not produce rulings and conclusions that conflict with their logic. Characteristics of intuition: Sayyid Ahmad Uthman in 1966 conducted a psychological experiment on intuitive thinking and reached the following: 1. The research results indicate that intuition is closer to the extroversion trait in personality than introversion. 2. Speed of performance, not immediacy. 3. Intuition is not related to conformity behavior or social norms. 4. There is a relationship between intuition and animism. 5. Intuitive thinking is closer to optimism than pessimism. 6. The process of intuition is integrative with other types of thinking such as correlation, flexibility, and inference. 7. Intuition is not related to pure wild guess, meaning the common concept of intuition as guesswork has no scientific basis. 8. Individuals with intuitive thinking are more controlled, emotionally balanced, and responsible. Some researchers wanted to summarize these characteristics and summarized them in three points: 1. Direct knowledge that needs no intermediaries and has no gradation. 2. Direct transition to the core of the known subject instead of presenting external or superficial descriptions of the subject, or limiting knowledge of it through comparison with others. 3. Individual knowledge that is not transmitted to others and cannot be taught or generalized. The Quran's stance on intuition: Before initiating the recording of what appears to be the Quran's stance on intuitive thinking as a source for obtaining knowledge, I think it is not objective to ignore the great influence of Henri Bergson, who is considered the founder of this trend in the present era. He has led many contemporary researchers to determine their stance on intuition in light of Bergson's vision. The truth is, whatever the distinguished interest of Henri Bergson in intuition, to the point that he became the owner of a theory worthy of study, that does not make his study a general consistent criterion, because the biggest factor of objective criticism directed at his theory – from the perspective of the Islamic conception – is that it is based far from the guidance of revelation and its directions.
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological discussion on intuition as a secondary source of knowledge. The author begins by affirming that intuition retains its importance in knowledge acquisition, provided it does not contradict scientific thinking or reliable sources like reason. When it opposes them, it becomes superstitious. Otherwise, intuition is valid in domains where revelation, sense, and reason are limited due to insufficient information. The author then lists eight characteristics of intuition based on a psychological study by Sayyid Ahmad Uthman (1966). These include: intuition is linked to extroversion, involves speed but not immediacy, is unrelated to social conformity, correlates with animism, inclines toward optimism, integrates with other thinking types, is distinct from wild guessing, and intuitives are more controlled and responsible. Subsequently, some researchers summarized these traits into three core features: directness without mediation, immediate grasping of the subject's essence, and individuality (non-transferable and non-generalizable). Finally, the author addresses the Quranic stance on intuition, cautioning against the overwhelming influence of Henri Bergson's theory. While Bergson's work is significant, the author argues that his perspective cannot serve as a universal standard from an Islamic viewpoint because it operates independently of divine revelation. Thus, the Quranic position must be understood through the lens of revelation's guidance.

Key Terms
الحدس
المصادر التبعية
التفكير الخرافي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, under what condition does intuition become superstitious thinking?
A) When it is used in fields with insufficient information.
B) When it contradicts reliable sources like reason and scientific thinking.
C) When it is integrative with other types of thinking.
D) When it is characterized by speed of performance.

Key Takeaway
Intuition is a valid secondary source only when it does not contradict revelation, sense, or reason.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider a scenario: A scholar has an intuitive feeling that a certain contract is permissible. Using the conditions from this passage, list which primary sources (revelation, sense, reason) you would check to validate this intuition. Give an example where the intuition would be rejected because it contradicts one of these sources.

Characteristics of Intuition from a Psychological Study
Author reports psychological findings on intuition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list and explain the eight characteristics of intuition from the 1966 study and the three summarized traits.

Core Idea
Intuition is a direct, fast, individual, and integrated cognitive process, not wild guesswork.

The passage presents a psychological study that identifies eight characteristics of intuitive thinking, later condensed into three core features. This lesson breaks down these traits, helping you understand what intuition is and what it is not. This scientific description complements the Islamic epistemological framework.

Guided Path
1
Read the eight characteristics listed in the study
Scan the points from the passage. Note each characteristic: extroversion, speed (not immediacy), no relation to conformity, link to animism, optimism, integration with other thinking, not wild guess, and emotional balance.
The term 'immediacy' in parentheses may be a translation issue; the author distinguishes speed from immediacy.
2
Identify the three summarized traits
After the list, researchers summarized them into three: direct knowledge without intermediaries, immediate grasp of essence, and individuality (non-transferable).
3
Distinguish intuition from wild guess
Point 7 explicitly states intuition is not wild guessing. Emphasize that this corrects a common misconception.
4
Connect to Islamic sciences
Consider how these traits appear in Islamic scholarship: e.g., a mujtahid might have an intuitive grasp of a ruling after deep study, which is direct and individual but not guesswork.

الباب الثالث: الفصل الرابع - المصادر التبعية
والواقع أن تقييدهم هذا لا يقلل من أهمية الحدس في عملية المعرفة، كما لا يشكك في سلامة التفكير الحدسي، إلا حينما يقف عقبة – بالفعل – أمام التفكير العلمي، ومصادماً للمصادر والطرائق المعتبرة كالعقل مثلاً، وفي هذه الحال يستحيل الحدس إلى ضرب من التفكير الخرافي المرفوض. أما فيما عدا هذه الحال فإني لا أذهب بعيداً إذا ما اعتبرته عاماً صالحاً لكل الميادين التي لا يعمل فيها أي من الوحي أو الحس أو العقل، نتيجة لقلة المعلومات المتاحة لنا فيها، إذ الحدس - في هذه الحال - إنما يستمد صدق استنتاجه بدعم منها حين يوافقها، ولا يأتي بأحكام واستنتاجات تتصادم مع منطقها.
خصائص الحدس
قام سيد أحمد عثمان سنة (١٩٦٦م) بإجراء تجربة نفسية حول التفكير الحدسي (Intuitive Thinking) وتوصل إلى ما يلي:
۱ تومئ نتائج البحث بأن الحدس أقرب إلى سمة الانبساط في الشخصية منه إلى الانطواء.
۲ - سرعة الأداء لا المباشرة (Immedicay).
- لا يرتبط الحدس بسلوك المسايرة أو المعايير الاجتماعية.
- ثمة علاقة بين الحدس والنزعة الإحيائية (animism).
ء - التفكير الحدسي أقرب إلى النزعة التفاؤلية منه إلى التشاؤمية. ٦ - عملية الحدس تكاملية مع بقية أنواع التفكير الأخرى كالعلاقة والمرونة والاستدلال.
لا يرتبط الحدس بالتخمين المحض Wild Guess أي إن المفهوم السائد عن الحدس بمعنى التخمين ليس له أساس علمي.
۸ - مجموعة الأفراد ذوو التفكير الحدسي (Intuitive Thinking) أكثر سيطرة واتزانا انفعاليا ومسؤولية.

١- معرفة مباشرة لا تحتاج إلى وسائط، ولا تدرّج فيها.
٢- الانتقال المباشر إلى لب الموضوع المعروف بدلا تقديمه أوصافاً من خارجية أو سطحية للموضوع، أو يقتصر على معرفته من خلال مقارنته بغيره.
٣- معرفة فردية لا تنتقل إلى الآخرين ولا يمكن تلقينها أو تعميمها.

Islamic Critique of Bergson's Theory of Intuition
Author critiques Bergson's theory of intuition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct the author's critique of Henri Bergson's theory of intuition from an Islamic perspective.

Core Idea
Bergson's intuition theory fails because it ignores divine revelation.

Henri Bergson's philosophy of intuition has heavily influenced modern thought, but from an Islamic standpoint it is fundamentally incomplete. The author argues that Bergson's theory, while valuable, cannot be a universal criterion because it operates without the guidance of revelation. This lesson unpacks that critique and helps you apply it to evaluate intuition-based claims.

Guided Path
1
Identify Bergson's role in the passage
The author mentions Bergson as the founder of the intuitionist trend in modern times and notes his significant influence on contemporary researchers.
2
Extract the author's criticism
The author states that Bergson's theory is not a 'general consistent criterion' because it is based far from the guidance of revelation (tawjeeh al-wahy). This is the core critique.
3
Understand the Islamic alternative
Implicitly, the author suggests that any valid theory of intuition must incorporate revelation as a guiding source. Intuition is acceptable only when it aligns with revealed knowledge.
This aligns with Lesson 1's conditions.
4
Apply the critique to a modern claim
Consider a popular intuition-based practice (e.g., 'follow your gut' for moral decisions). Evaluate it using the author's criterion: does it rely on revelation? If not, it may be insufficient from an Islamic perspective.
